	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Northwestern University</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other universities with a similar name, see <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Northwestern University (disambiguation)">Northwestern University (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Private research university in Illinois, United States</div>

<p><b>Northwestern University</b> (<b>NU</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">research university</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Evanston,_Illinois" title="Evanston, Illinois">Evanston, Illinois</a>, United States, with other campuses located in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_in_Qatar" title="Northwestern University in Qatar">Doha, Qatar</a>, and academic programs and facilities in <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami, Florida</a>; <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>; and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ugrad_program_list_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ugrad_program_list-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Grad_program_list_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grad_program_list-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Along with its selective undergraduate programs, Northwestern is known for its <a href="/wiki/Kellogg_School_of_Management_at_Northwestern_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Kellogg School of Management at Northwestern University">Kellogg School of Management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Pritzker_School_of_Law" title="Northwestern University Pritzker School of Law">Pritzker School of Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feinberg_School_of_Medicine" title="Feinberg School of Medicine">Feinberg School of Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bienen_School_of_Music" title="Bienen School of Music">Bienen School of Music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medill_School_of_Journalism" title="Medill School of Journalism">Medill School of Journalism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_R._McCormick_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Science" title="Robert R. McCormick School of Engineering and Applied Science">McCormick School of Engineering and Applied Science</a>.
</p><p>Northwestern is a large research university with a comprehensive doctoral program, attracting nearly $800 million in sponsored research each year.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> As of 2018, Northwestern has the tenth-largest university endowment in the United States, valued at a record $11.08 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-nacubo_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nacubo-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The university's former and present <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_faculty" title="List of Northwestern University faculty">faculty</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_alumni" title="List of Northwestern University alumni">alumni</a> include 19 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">Nobel Prize laureates</a>, 38 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> six <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellows_Program" title="MacArthur Fellows Program">MacArthur Genius</a> Fellows,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> 16 <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholars</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> 65 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a><sup id="cite_ref-acad_directory_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acad_directory-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and two <a href="/wiki/List_of_Justices_of_the_Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="List of Justices of the Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court Justices</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern's <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Communication" title="Northwestern University School of Communication">School of Communication</a> is a leading producer of <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">Tony Award</a>–winning actors, actresses, playwrights, writers and directors.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Northwestern was founded in 1851 by <a href="/wiki/John_Evans_(governor)" title="John Evans (governor)">John Evans</a>, for whom the city of Evanston is named, and eight other lawyers, businessmen and <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a> leaders. Its founding purpose was to serve the Old <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territory" title="Northwest Territory">Northwest Territory</a>, an area that includes the states of Ohio, Indiana, Illinois, Michigan, Wisconsin and parts of Minnesota.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Instruction began in 1855 and women were admitted in 1869. Today, the main campus is a 240-acre (97&#160;ha) parcel in Evanston, along the shores of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Michigan" title="Lake Michigan">Lake Michigan</a> 12 miles north of downtown Chicago. The university's <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Northwestern University School of Law">law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feinberg_School_of_Medicine" title="Feinberg School of Medicine">medical</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Professional_Studies" title="Northwestern University School of Professional Studies">professional</a> schools, along with its nationally ranked affiliated <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Memorial_Hospital" title="Northwestern Memorial Hospital">Northwestern Memorial Hospital</a>, are located on a 25-acre (10&#160;ha) campus in Chicago's <a href="/wiki/Streeterville" title="Streeterville">Streeterville</a> neighborhood. In 2008, the university opened a campus in <a href="/wiki/Education_City" title="Education City">Education City</a>, Doha, Qatar with programs in journalism and communication.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, Northwestern opened its San Francisco space at <a href="/wiki/44_Montgomery" title="44 Montgomery">44 Montgomery</a> St., which hosts journalism, engineering, and marketing programs.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The university is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> and remains the only private university in the conference.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats" title="Northwestern Wildcats">Northwestern Wildcats</a> compete in 19 intercollegiate sports in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">Division I</a> Big Ten Conference.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Northwestern_University" title="History of Northwestern University">History of Northwestern University</a></div>
<p>The foundation of Northwestern University can be traced to a meeting on May 31, 1850, of nine prominent Chicago businessmen, Methodist leaders, and attorneys who had formed the idea of establishing a university to serve what had been known from 1787 to 1803 as the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territory" title="Northwest Territory">Northwest Territory</a>. On January 28, 1851, the <a href="/wiki/Illinois_General_Assembly" title="Illinois General Assembly">Illinois General Assembly</a> granted a charter to the <i>Trustees of the North-Western University</i>, making it the first chartered university in Illinois.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Charter_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charter-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The school's nine founders, all of whom were Methodists (three of them <a href="/wiki/Elder_(Methodism)" class="mw-redirect" title="Elder (Methodism)">ministers</a>), knelt in <a href="/wiki/Prayer_in_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Prayer in Christianity">prayer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christian_worship" title="Christian worship">worship</a> before launching their first organizational meeting.<sup id="cite_ref-Northwestern_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Northwestern-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Although they affiliated the university with the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="Methodist Episcopal Church">Methodist Episcopal Church</a>, they favored a <a href="/wiki/Non-sectarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-sectarian">non-sectarian</a> admissions policy, believing that Northwestern should serve all people in the newly developing territory by bettering the economy in Evanston.<sup id="cite_ref-Planning_a_university_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Planning_a_university-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg/220px-University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg/330px-University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg/440px-University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3880" data-file-height="2586" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>University Hall (1869), the second building constructed on campus, and the oldest building still standing</div></div></div>
<p>John Evans, for whom Evanston is named, bought 379 acres (153&#160;ha) of land along Lake Michigan in 1853, and Philo Judson developed plans for what would become the city of <a href="/wiki/Evanston,_Illinois" title="Evanston, Illinois">Evanston, Illinois</a>. The first building, <a href="/wiki/Old_College,_Northwestern_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Old College, Northwestern University">Old College</a>, opened on November 5, 1855.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> To raise funds for its construction, Northwestern sold $100 "perpetual scholarships" entitling the purchaser and his heirs to free tuition.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Perpetual_scholarships_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perpetual_scholarships-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Another building, <a href="/wiki/University_Hall_(Northwestern_University)" title="University Hall (Northwestern University)">University Hall</a>, was built in 1869 of the same Joliet limestone as the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Water_Tower" title="Chicago Water Tower">Chicago Water Tower</a>, also built in 1869, one of the few buildings in the heart of Chicago to survive the <a href="/wiki/Great_Chicago_Fire" title="Great Chicago Fire">Great Chicago Fire</a> of 1871.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In 1873 the <a href="/wiki/Evanston_College_for_Ladies" title="Evanston College for Ladies">Evanston College for Ladies</a> merged with Northwestern, and <a href="/wiki/Frances_Willard_(suffragist)" class="mw-redirect" title="Frances Willard (suffragist)">Frances Willard</a>, who later gained fame as a <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage" title="Women&#39;s suffrage">suffragette</a> and as one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/Woman%27s_Christian_Temperance_Union" title="Woman&#39;s Christian Temperance Union">Woman's Christian Temperance Union</a> (WCTU), became the school's first <a href="/wiki/Dean_of_women" title="Dean of women">dean of women</a>. (<a href="/wiki/Willard_Residential_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Willard Residential College">Willard Residential College</a> (1938) honors her name.) Northwestern admitted its first female students in 1869, and the first woman was graduated in 1874.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
Northwestern fielded its first intercollegiate football team in 1882, later becoming a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a>. In the 1870s and 1880s, Northwestern affiliated itself with already existing schools of law, medicine, and dentistry in Chicago. <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Pritzker_School_of_Law" title="Northwestern University Pritzker School of Law">Northwestern University Pritzker School of Law</a> is the oldest law school in Chicago. As the university increased in wealth and distinction, and enrollments grew, these professional schools were integrated with the undergraduate college in Evanston; the result was a modern research-university combining professional, graduate, and undergraduate programs, which gave equal weight to teaching and to research.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> invited Northwestern to become a member in 1917. </p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Deering_front.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Deering_front.jpg/220px-Deering_front.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="82" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Deering_front.jpg/330px-Deering_front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Deering_front.jpg/440px-Deering_front.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="1449" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Deering_front.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Deering Library (1933)</div></div></div>
<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Walter_Dill_Scott" title="Walter Dill Scott">Walter Dill Scott</a>'s presidency from 1920 to 1939, Northwestern began construction of an integrated campus in Chicago designed by <a href="/wiki/James_Gamble_Rogers" title="James Gamble Rogers">James Gamble Rogers</a> to house the professional schools; established the <a href="/wiki/Kellogg_School_of_Management" title="Kellogg School of Management">Kellogg School of Management</a>; and built several prominent buildings on the Evanston campus, <a href="/wiki/Dyche_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Dyche Stadium">Dyche Stadium</a> (now named Ryan Field) and <a href="/wiki/Deering_Library" title="Deering Library">Deering Library</a> among others. In 1933 a proposal to merge Northwestern with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a> was considered but rejected.<sup id="cite_ref-Barnes_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barnes-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UChicago_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UChicago-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern became one of the first six universities in the United States to establish a <a href="/wiki/Naval_Reserve_Officers_Training_Corps" title="Naval Reserve Officers Training Corps">Naval Reserve Officers Training Corps</a> (NROTC) in the 1920s. Northwestern played host to the first-ever <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA Men&#39;s Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship</a> game in 1939 in the original <a href="/wiki/Patten_Gymnasium" title="Patten Gymnasium">Patten Gymnasium</a>, which was later demolished and relocated farther north along with the <a href="/wiki/Dearborn_Observatory" title="Dearborn Observatory">Dearborn Observatory</a> to make room for the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Technological_Institute" title="Northwestern Technological Institute">Technological Institute</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TechInstitute-PreLakefill.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/TechInstitute-PreLakefill.jpg/320px-TechInstitute-PreLakefill.jpg" decoding="async" width="320" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/TechInstitute-PreLakefill.jpg/480px-TechInstitute-PreLakefill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/TechInstitute-PreLakefill.jpg/640px-TechInstitute-PreLakefill.jpg 2x" data-file-width="956" data-file-height="785" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TechInstitute-PreLakefill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Technological Institute in 1942, after the relocation of Patten Gymnasium but before the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Lakefill" title="Northwestern University Lakefill">Lakefill</a></div></div></div>
<p>After the golden years of the 1920s, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression_in_the_United_States" title="Great Depression in the United States">Great Depression in the United States</a> (1929–1941) hit Northwestern hard. Its annual income dropped 25 percent from $4.8 million in 1930-31 to $3.6 million in 1933-34. Investment income shrank, fewer people could pay full tuition, and annual giving from  alumni and philanthropy fell from $870,000 in 1932 to a low of  $331,000 in 1935. The university responded with two salary cuts of 10 percent each for all employees. It imposed a hiring freeze, a building freeze, and slashed appropriations for maintenance, books, and research. Having had a balanced budget in 1930-31, the university now faced deficits of roughly $100,000 for the next four years, which was made up by using the endowment. Enrollments fell in most schools, with law and music suffering the biggest declines. But the movement toward state certification of school teachers prompted Northwestern to start a new graduate program in education, thereby bringing in new students and much needed income. In June 1933, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Maynard_Hutchins" title="Robert Maynard Hutchins">Robert Maynard Hutchins</a>, president of the University of Chicago, proposed a merger of the two universities, estimating annual savings of $1.7 million. The two presidents were enthusiastic, and the faculty liked the idea; the Northwestern alumni, however, opposed it, fearing the loss of their Alma Mater and its many traditions that distinguished Northwestern from Chicago. The medical school, for example, was oriented toward training practitioners, and feared it would lose its mission if it were merged into the larger, more research-oriented <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Medical_School" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Chicago Medical School">University of Chicago Medical School</a>.  The merger plan was dropped.  The <a href="/wiki/Charles_Deering" title="Charles Deering">Deering</a> family gave an unrestricted gift of $6 million in 1935 that rescued the budget, bringing it up to $5.4 million in 1938-39. That allowed many of the spending cuts to be restored, including  half the salary reductions.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Like other American research universities, Northwestern was transformed by <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> (1939–1945). The regular enrollment fell dramatically, but the school opened high-intensity, short-term courses that trained over 50,000 military personnel.  <a href="/wiki/Franklyn_B._Snyder" class="mw-redirect" title="Franklyn B. Snyder">Franklyn B. Snyder</a> led the university from 1939 to 1949, and after the war, surging enrollments under the <a href="/wiki/G.I._Bill" title="G.I. Bill">G.I. Bill</a> drove dramatic expansion of both campuses. In 1948 prominent anthropologist <a href="/wiki/Melville_J._Herskovits" title="Melville J. Herskovits">Melville J. Herskovits</a> founded the Program of <a href="/wiki/African_studies" title="African studies">African Studies</a> at Northwestern, the first center of its kind at an American academic institution.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/J._Roscoe_Miller" title="J. Roscoe Miller">J. Roscoe Miller</a>'s tenure as president from 1949 to 1970 saw the expansion of the Evanston campus, with the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Lakefill" class="mw-redirect" title="Lakefill">lakefill</a> on Lake Michigan, growth of the faculty and new academic programs, as well as polarizing Vietnam-era student protests. In 1978 the first and second <a href="/wiki/Unabomber" class="mw-redirect" title="Unabomber">Unabomber</a> attacks occurred at Northwestern University.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Relations between Evanston and Northwestern became strained throughout much of the post-war era because of episodes of disruptive student activism,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> disputes over municipal zoning, building codes, and law enforcement,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> as well as restrictions on the sale of alcohol near campus until 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dry_campus_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dry_campus-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern's exemption from state and municipal property-tax obligations under its original charter has historically been a source of <a href="/wiki/Town_and_gown" title="Town and gown">town-and-gown</a> tension.  In the 2010s, a 5-year capital campaign resulted in a new music center, a new replacement-building for the business school, and a $270 million athletic complex.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Though government support for universities declined in the 1970s and 1980s, President <a href="/wiki/Arnold_R._Weber" title="Arnold R. Weber">Arnold R. Weber</a> was able to stabilize university finances, leading to a revitalization of the campuses. As admissions to colleges and universities grew increasingly competitive in the 1990s and 2000s, President <a href="/wiki/Henry_S._Bienen" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry S. Bienen">Henry S. Bienen</a>'s tenure saw a notable increase in the number and quality of undergraduate applicants, continued expansion of the facilities and faculty, and renewed athletic competitiveness. In 1999, Northwestern student journalists uncovered information exonerating Illinois <a href="/wiki/Death-row" class="mw-redirect" title="Death-row">death-row</a> inmate <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Porter" title="Anthony Porter">Anthony Porter</a> two days before his scheduled execution, and the Innocence Project has since exonerated 10 more men.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On January 11, 2003, in a speech at Northwestern School of Law's Lincoln Hall, then <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Illinois" title="Governor of Illinois">Governor of Illinois</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Ryan" title="George Ryan">George Ryan</a> announced that he would <a href="/wiki/Commutation_of_sentence" class="mw-redirect" title="Commutation of sentence">commute</a> the sentences of more than 150 death-row inmates.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> phrase on Northwestern's seal, <i>Quaecumque sunt vera</i> ("Whatsoever things are true") is drawn from the <a href="/wiki/Epistle_to_the_Philippians" title="Epistle to the Philippians">Epistle of Paul to the Philippians</a> (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Philippians#4:8" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/Philippians">Philippians 4:8</a>), while the Greek phrase inscribed on the pages of an open book is taken from the <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_John" title="Gospel of John">Gospel of John</a>: <i>ο λόγος πλήρης χάριτος και αληθείας</i> ("The Word full of grace and truth", <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/John#1:14" class="extiw" title="s:Bible (King James)/John">John 1:14</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Faith_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faith-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Seal_history_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seal_history-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Purple" title="Purple">Purple</a> became Northwestern's official color in 1892,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> replacing <a href="/wiki/Black" title="Black">black</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gold_(color)" title="Gold (color)">gold</a> after a university committee concluded that too many other universities had used these colors. Today, Northwestern's official color is purple, although white is something of an official color as well, being mentioned in both the university's earliest song, <i>Alma Mater</i> (1907) ("Hail to purple, hail to white") and in many university guidelines.<sup id="cite_ref-purple_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-purple-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-School_colors_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-School_colors-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_buildings" title="List of Northwestern University buildings">List of Northwestern University buildings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Campus_of_Northwestern_University" title="Campus of Northwestern University">Campus of Northwestern University</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evanston">Evanston</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Evanston">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg/220px-Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="80" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg/330px-Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg/440px-Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3253" data-file-height="1179" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Northwestern's Evanston campus is located on <a href="/wiki/Lake_Michigan" title="Lake Michigan">Lake Michigan</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Northwestern's Evanston campus, where the undergraduate schools, the Graduate School, and the Kellogg School of Management are located, runs north-south from Lincoln Avenue to Clark Street west of Lake Michigan along  <a href="/wiki/Sheridan_Road" title="Sheridan Road">Sheridan Road</a>. North and South Campuses have noticeably different atmospheres, owing to the predominance of Science and Athletics in the one and Humanities and Arts in the other. North Campus is home to the <a href="/wiki/Fraternity_and_sorority_houses" class="mw-redirect" title="Fraternity and sorority houses">fraternity</a> <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(architecture)" title="Quadrangle (architecture)">quads</a>, the Henry Crown Sports Pavilion and Norris Aquatics Center and other athletic facilities, the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Technological_Institute" title="Northwestern Technological Institute">Technological Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dearborn_Observatory" title="Dearborn Observatory">Dearborn Observatory</a>, and other science-related buildings including Patrick G. and Shirley W. Ryan Hall for Nanofabrication and Molecular Self-Assembly, and the Ford Motor Company Engineering Design Center. South Campus is home to the university's humanities buildings, <a href="/wiki/Pick-Staiger_Concert_Hall" title="Pick-Staiger Concert Hall">Pick-Staiger Concert Hall</a> and other music buildings, the <a href="/wiki/Mary_and_Leigh_Block_Museum_of_Art" title="Mary and Leigh Block Museum of Art">Mary and Leigh Block Museum of Art</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Fraternity_and_sorority_houses" class="mw-redirect" title="Fraternity and sorority houses">sorority</a> quads.  In the 1960s, the university created an additional 84 acres (34.0&#160;ha) by means of a lakefill in Lake Michigan. Among some of the buildings located on these broad new acres are University Library, <a href="/wiki/Norris_University_Center" title="Norris University Center">Norris University Center</a> (the student union), and <a href="/wiki/Pick-Staiger_Concert_Hall" title="Pick-Staiger Concert Hall">Pick-Staiger Concert Hall</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Transit_Authority" title="Chicago Transit Authority">Chicago Transit Authority</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Chicago_%27L%27" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago &#39;L&#39;">elevated train</a> running through Evanston is called the <a href="/wiki/Purple_Line_(Chicago_Transit_Authority)" class="mw-redirect" title="Purple Line (Chicago Transit Authority)">Purple Line</a>, taking its name from Northwestern's school color. The <a href="/wiki/Foster_(CTA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Foster (CTA)">Foster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Davis_(CTA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Davis (CTA)">Davis</a> stations are within walking distance of the southern end of the campus, while the <a href="/wiki/Noyes_(CTA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Noyes (CTA)">Noyes</a> station is close to the northern end of the campus. The <a href="/wiki/Central_(CTA_Purple_Line)" class="mw-redirect" title="Central (CTA Purple Line)">Central</a> station is close to <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Field_(stadium)" title="Ryan Field (stadium)">Ryan Field</a>, Northwestern's football stadium.  The <a href="/wiki/Evanston_Davis_Street_(Metra)" class="mw-redirect" title="Evanston Davis Street (Metra)">Evanston Davis Street</a> <a href="/wiki/Metra" title="Metra">Metra</a> station serves the Northwestern campus in downtown Evanston and the <a href="/wiki/Evanston_Central_Street_(Metra)" class="mw-redirect" title="Evanston Central Street (Metra)">Evanston Central Street</a> Metra station is near Ryan Field. Pace Suburban Bus Service and the CTA have several bus routes that run through or near the Evanston campus.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG" class="image" title="Panorama of Northwestern University"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG/800px-Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG" decoding="async" width="800" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG/1200px-Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG/1600px-Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG 2x" data-file-width="3535" data-file-height="690" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG" title="File:Northwestern University lakefill panorama.PNG"> </a></div>Panorama of Northwestern University</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chicago">Chicago</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Chicago">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ward_Building_060527.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ward_Building_060527.jpg/220px-Ward_Building_060527.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ward_Building_060527.jpg/330px-Ward_Building_060527.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ward_Building_060527.jpg/440px-Ward_Building_060527.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="824" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ward_Building_060527.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Montgomery Ward Memorial Building (1927) at Northwestern's Feinberg School of Medicine in Chicago, America's first academic skyscraper<sup id="cite_ref-WardBuilding_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WardBuilding-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Northwestern's Chicago campus is located in the city's <a href="/wiki/Streeterville" title="Streeterville">Streeterville</a> neighborhood. The Chicago campus is home to the nationally ranked and affiliated <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Memorial_Hospital" title="Northwestern Memorial Hospital">Northwestern Memorial Hospital</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Feinberg_School_of_Medicine" title="Feinberg School of Medicine">medical school</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Northwestern University School of Law">law school</a>, the part-time <a href="/wiki/MBA" class="mw-redirect" title="MBA">MBA</a> program, and the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Professional_Studies" title="Northwestern University School of Professional Studies">School of Professional Studies</a>. Northwestern's professional schools and affiliated hospitals are about four blocks east of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_(CTA_Red_Line)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago (CTA Red Line)">Chicago</a> station on the CTA <a href="/wiki/Red_Line_(Chicago_Transit_Authority)" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Line (Chicago Transit Authority)">Red Line</a>. The Chicago campus is also served by CTA bus routes.
</p><p>Founded at various times in the university's history, the professional schools originally were scattered throughout Chicago.<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_Campus_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago_Campus-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In connection with a 1917 master plan for a central Chicago campus and President <a href="/wiki/Walter_Dill_Scott" title="Walter Dill Scott">Walter Dill Scott</a>'s capital campaign, 8.5 acres (3.44&#160;ha) of land were purchased at the corner of <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Avenue" title="Chicago Avenue">Chicago Avenue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Shore_Drive" title="Lake Shore Drive">Lake Shore Drive</a> for $1.5 million in 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_Campus_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago_Campus-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_Campus_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago_Campus-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The architect <a href="/wiki/James_Gamble_Rogers" title="James Gamble Rogers">James Gamble Rogers</a> was commissioned to create a master plan for the principal buildings on the new campus which he designed in  <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_gothic" class="mw-redirect" title="Collegiate gothic">collegiate gothic</a> style. In 1923, <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Montgomery_Ward" title="Aaron Montgomery Ward">Mrs. Montgomery Ward</a> donated $8 million to the campaign to finance the construction of the Montgomery Ward Memorial Building which would house the medical and dental schools and to create endowments for faculty chairs, research grants, scholarships, and building maintenance.<sup id="cite_ref-Montgomery_Ward_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Montgomery_Ward-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The building would become the first university <a href="/wiki/Skyscraper" title="Skyscraper">skyscraper</a> in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-WardBuilding_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WardBuilding-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the Ward Building, Rogers designed <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_buildings#Wieboldt_Hall" title="List of Northwestern University buildings">Wieboldt Hall</a> to house facilities for the <a href="/wiki/Kellogg_School_of_Management#History" title="Kellogg School of Management">School of Commerce</a><sup id="cite_ref-Wieboldt_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wieboldt-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_buildings#Levy_Mayer_Hall" title="List of Northwestern University buildings">Levy Mayer Hall</a> to house the School of Law.<sup id="cite_ref-Levy_Mayer_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levy_Mayer-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The new campus comprising these three new buildings was dedicated during a two-day ceremony in June 1927. The Chicago campus continued to expand with the addition of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_buildings#Thorne_Hall" title="List of Northwestern University buildings">Thorne Hall</a> in 1931 and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_buildings#Abbott_Hall" title="List of Northwestern University buildings">Abbott Hall</a> in 1939.<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_Campus_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago_Campus-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Abbott_Hall_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abbott_Hall-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In October 2013, Northwestern began the demolition of the architecturally significant Prentice Women's Hospital. Eric G. Neilson, dean of the medical school, penned an op-ed that equated retaining the building with loss of life.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite_campus_in_Qatar">Satellite campus in Qatar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Satellite campus in Qatar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Fall 2008, Northwestern opened a campus in <a href="/wiki/Education_City" title="Education City">Education City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, joining five other American universities: <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University" title="Texas A&amp;M University">Texas A&amp;M University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="Virginia Commonwealth University">Virginia Commonwealth University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-meivy_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meivy-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Through the <a href="/wiki/Medill_School_of_Journalism" title="Medill School of Journalism">Medill School of Journalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Communication" title="Northwestern University School of Communication">School of Communication</a>, NU-Q offers <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor&#39;s degree">bachelor's degrees</a> in journalism and communication respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> However, some have questioned whether NU-Q can truly offer a comparable journalism program to that of its U.S. campus given Qatar’s strict limits on journalistic and academic freedoms and instances of <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">censorship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Foundation_for_Education,_Science_and_Community_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Qatar Foundation for Education, Science and Community Development">Qatar Foundation for Education, Science and Community Development</a>, a private charitable institution started by former emir <a href="/wiki/Hamad_bin_Khalifa_Al_Thani" title="Hamad bin Khalifa Al Thani">Sheikh Hamad bin Khalifa Al Thani</a> and his wife and mother of the current emir <a href="/wiki/Moza_bint_Nasser" title="Moza bint Nasser">Sheikha Moza bint Nasser</a>, provided funding for construction and administrative costs as well as support to hire 50 to 60 faculty and staff, some of whom rotate between the Evanston and Qatar campuses.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern receives about $45 million per year to operate the campus.<sup id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In February 2016, Northwestern reached an agreement with the Qatar Foundation to extend the operations of the NU-Q branch for an additional decade, through the 2027–2028 academic year.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> As with other universities with campuses in Doha, Northwestern has received criticism for accepting money from a country with poor human rights record.<sup id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Green_Power_Partnership" title="Green Power Partnership">Green Power Partnership</a> (sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/EPA" class="mw-redirect" title="EPA">EPA</a>) listed Northwestern as one of the top 10 universities in the country in purchasing energy from renewable sources. The university matches 74 million <a href="/wiki/Kilowatt_hour" title="Kilowatt hour">kilowatt hours</a> (kWh) of its annual energy use with Green-e Certified <a href="/wiki/Renewable_Energy_Certificate" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewable Energy Certificate">Renewable Energy Certificates</a> (RECs). This green power commitment represents 30 percent of the university's total annual electricity use and places Northwestern in the EPA's Green Power Leadership Club. The 2010 Report by The Sustainable Endowments Institute awarded Northwestern a "B-" on its College Sustainability Report Card.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The Initiative for Sustainability and Energy at Northwestern (ISEN), supporting research, teaching and outreach in these themes, was launched in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-ISEN_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISEN-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Northwestern requires that all new buildings be <a href="/wiki/LEED-certified" class="mw-redirect" title="LEED-certified">LEED-certified</a>. Silverman Hall on the Evanston campus was awarded Gold LEED Certification in 2010; Wieboldt Hall on the Chicago campus was awarded Gold LEED Certification in 2007, and the Ford Motor Company Engineering Design Center on the Evanston campus was awarded Silver LEED Certification in 2006. New construction and renovation projects will be designed to provide at least a 20% improvement over energy code requirements where technically feasible.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The university also released at the beginning of the 2008–09 academic year the Evanston Campus Framework Plan, which outlines plans for future development of the Evanston Campus. The plan not only emphasizes the sustainable construction of buildings, but also discusses improving transportation by optimizing pedestrian and bicycle access.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern has had a comprehensive <a href="/wiki/Recycling" title="Recycling">recycling</a> program in place since 1990. More than 1,500 tons are recycled annually at Northwestern, which represents 30% of the waste produced on campus. All landscape waste at the university is composted.<sup id="cite_ref-ISEN_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISEN-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_administration">Organization and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Organization and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_Arch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Northwestern_Arch.jpg/220px-Northwestern_Arch.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Northwestern_Arch.jpg/330px-Northwestern_Arch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Northwestern_Arch.jpg/440px-Northwestern_Arch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="992" data-file-height="623" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_Arch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Weber Arch</div></div></div>
<p>Northwestern is privately owned and is governed by an appointed <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Trustees" class="mw-redirect" title="Board of Trustees">Board of Trustees</a>. The board, composed of 70 members and as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> chaired by <a href="/wiki/William_A._Osborn" title="William A. Osborn">William A. Osborn</a> '69, delegates its power to an elected president to serve as the <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">chief executive officer</a> of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern has had <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_presidents" title="List of Northwestern University presidents">sixteen presidents in its history</a> (excluding interim presidents), the current president, <a href="/wiki/Morton_O._Schapiro" title="Morton O. Schapiro">Morton O. Schapiro</a>, an economist, having succeeded <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bienen" title="Henry Bienen">Henry Bienen</a> whose 14-year tenure ended on August 31, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The president has a staff of vice presidents, directors, and other assistants for administrative, financial, faculty, and student matters.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Holloway_(historian)" title="Jonathan Holloway (historian)">Jonathan Holloway</a>, provost since August 2017, serves under the president as the <a href="/wiki/Chief_academic_officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief academic officer">chief academic officer</a> of the university to whom the deans of every academic school, leaders of cross-disciplinary units, and chairs of the standing faculty committee report.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students&#39; union">Associated Student Government</a> consists of the elected representatives of the undergraduate students and the Graduate Student Association represents graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Northwestern University is composed of 12 schools and colleges. The faculty for each school consists of the dean of the school and the instructional faculty. Faculty are responsible for teaching, research, advising students, and serving on committees. Each school's admission requirements, degree requirements, courses of study, and disciplinary and degree recommendations are determined by the voting members of that school's faculty (assistant professor and above).<sup id="cite_ref-Faculty_handbook_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faculty_handbook-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2003, Northwestern finished a five-year capital campaign that raised $1.55 billion, $550 million more than its goal. In 2007, the university sold its royalty interest in the pain relief drug <a href="/wiki/Lyrica" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyrica">Lyrica</a> for $700 million, a drug developed at Northwestern by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Bruce_Silverman" title="Richard Bruce Silverman">Richard Bruce Silverman</a> (for whom Silverman Hall was named), who is the John Evans Professor of Chemistry. This was the largest such sale in history,<sup id="cite_ref-Lyrica_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyrica-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> the proceeds of which were added to the endowment.<sup id="cite_ref-Financial_Report_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Financial_Report-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, Northwestern announced the "We Will Campaign" with a fundraising goal of $3.75 billion. As of February 28, 2017, the university has received $3.31 billion towards its goal.
</p>

<p>Northwestern University had a dental school from 1891 to May 31, 2001, when it closed.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings">Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div>
