<p>Northwestern is a large, residential <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">research university</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Higher_education_accreditation" title="Higher education accreditation">Accredited</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Higher_Learning_Commission" title="Higher Learning Commission">Higher Learning Commission</a> and the respective national professional organizations for chemistry, psychology, business, education, journalism, music, engineering, law, and medicine,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> the university offers 124 undergraduate programs and 145 graduate and professional programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Ugrad_program_list_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ugrad_program_list-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Grad_program_list_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grad_program_list-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern conferred 2,190 bachelor's degrees, 3,272 master's degrees, 565 doctoral degrees, and 444 <a href="/wiki/Professional_degree" title="Professional degree">professional degrees</a> in 2012–2013.<sup id="cite_ref-ourstudents_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ourstudents-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The four-year, full-time undergraduate program comprises the majority of enrollments at the university and emphasizes instruction in the arts and sciences, plus the professions of engineering, journalism, communication, music, and education.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Although a foundation in the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberal arts">liberal arts</a> and sciences is required in all majors, there is no required common <a href="/wiki/Core_curriculum" class="mw-redirect" title="Core curriculum">core curriculum</a>; individual degree requirements are set by the faculty of each school.<sup id="cite_ref-Faculty_handbook_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faculty_handbook-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern's full-time undergraduate and graduate programs operate on an approximately 10-week <a href="/wiki/Academic_quarter_(year_division)" title="Academic quarter (year division)">academic quarter system</a> with the academic year beginning in late September and ending in early June. Undergraduates typically take four courses each quarter and twelve courses in an academic year and<sup id="cite_ref-Catalog_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalog-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> are required to complete at least twelve quarters on campus to graduate. Northwestern offers honors, accelerated, and joint degree programs in medicine, science, mathematics, engineering, and journalism.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The comprehensive doctoral graduate program has high coexistence with undergraduate programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Undergraduates with <a href="/wiki/Grade_point_average" class="mw-redirect" title="Grade point average">grade point averages</a> in the highest five percent of each graduating class are awarded degrees <i><a href="/wiki/Latin_honors" title="Latin honors">summa cum laude</a></i>, the next eight percent <i>magna cum laude</i>, and the next twelve percent <i>cum laude</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Honors_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Honors-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern also has chapters of academic honor societies such as <a href="/wiki/Phi_Beta_Kappa" title="Phi Beta Kappa">Phi Beta Kappa</a> (Alpha of Illinois), <a href="/wiki/Eta_Kappa_Nu" title="Eta Kappa Nu">Eta Kappa Nu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tau_Beta_Pi" title="Tau Beta Pi">Tau Beta Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eta_Sigma_Phi" title="Eta Sigma Phi">Eta Sigma Phi</a> (Beta Chapter),<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lambda_Pi_Eta" title="Lambda Pi Eta">Lambda Pi Eta</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Honors_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Honors-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Sigma_Lambda" title="Alpha Sigma Lambda">Alpha Sigma Lambda</a> (Alpha Chapter).<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Since 1951, Northwestern has awarded 520 <a href="/wiki/Honorary_degrees" class="mw-redirect" title="Honorary degrees">honorary degrees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Undergraduate cost of attendance for the 2012/13 school year was $61,240; this includes the basic tuition of $43,380, fees (health $200, etc.), room and board of $13,329 (less if commuting), books and supplies $1,842, personal expenses $1,890, transportation cost of $400.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalog-FinAid_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalog-FinAid-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern awards financial aid solely on the basis of need through loans, work-study, grants, and scholarships.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalog-FinAid_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalog-FinAid-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FinAid_FAQ_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FinAid_FAQ-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The university processed in excess of $472 million in financial aid for the 2009–2010 academic year. This included $265 million in institutional funds, with the remainder coming from federal and state governments and private organizations and individuals. Northwestern scholarship programs for undergraduate students support needy students from a variety of income and backgrounds. Approximately 44 percent of the June 2010 graduates had received federal and/or private loans for their undergraduate education, graduating with an average debt of $17,200.
</p><p>In the fall of 2014, among the six undergraduate schools, 40.6% of undergraduate students are enrolled in the <a href="/wiki/Weinberg_College_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Weinberg College of Arts and Sciences">Weinberg College of Arts and Sciences</a>, 21.3% in the <a href="/wiki/Robert_R._McCormick_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Science" title="Robert R. McCormick School of Engineering and Applied Science">McCormick School of Engineering and Applied Science</a>, 14.3% in the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Communication" title="Northwestern University School of Communication">School of Communication</a>, 11.7% in the <a href="/wiki/Medill_School_of_Journalism" title="Medill School of Journalism">Medill School of Journalism</a>, 5.7% in the <a href="/wiki/Bienen_School_of_Music" title="Bienen School of Music">Bienen School of Music</a>, and 6.4% in the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Education_and_Social_Policy" title="Northwestern University School of Education and Social Policy">School of Education and Social Policy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Enrollments_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Enrollments-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The five most commonly awarded undergraduate degrees are in economics, journalism, communication studies, psychology, and political science.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> While professional students are affiliated with their respective schools, the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Professional_Studies" title="Northwestern University School of Professional Studies">School of Professional Studies</a> offers master's and bachelor's degree, and certificate programs tailored to the professional studies.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> With 2,446 students enrolled in science, engineering, and health fields,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> the largest graduate programs by enrollment include chemistry, integrated biology, material sciences, electrical and computer engineering, neuroscience, and economics.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kellogg_School_of_Management" title="Kellogg School of Management">Kellogg School of Management</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Business_Administration" title="Master of Business Administration">MBA</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Northwestern University School of Law">School of Law</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">JD</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Feinberg_School_of_Medicine" title="Feinberg School of Medicine">Feinberg School of Medicine</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">MD</a> are the three largest <a href="/wiki/First_professional_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="First professional degree">professional degree</a> programs by enrollment.<sup id="cite_ref-Enrollments_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Enrollments-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Admissions are characterized as "most selective" by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> There were 40,425 applications for the undergraduate class of 2022 (entering 2018). For early decision, 1,072 out of 4,049 applicants were admitted, for an acceptance rate of 26%. In regular decision, 2,320 out of 36,518 applicants were admitted, for an acceptance rate of 6.35%. In total, 3,392 out of 40,425 applicants were admitted for an overall acceptance rate of 8.4%, making Northwestern one of the most selective schools in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-dailynorthwestern.com_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dailynorthwestern.com-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> For freshmen enrolling in the class of 2021, the <a href="/wiki/Interquartile_range" title="Interquartile range">interquartile range</a> (middle 50%) on the post-2016 <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> was a combined (verbal and math) 1420-1560 out of 1600, <a href="/wiki/ACT_(examination)" class="mw-redirect" title="ACT (examination)">ACT</a> composite scores for the middle 50% ranged from 32 to 35 out of 36, and 91% ranked in the top ten percent of their respective high school classes.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2016, Northwestern announced that it signed on to the Chicago Star Partnership, a City Colleges initiative. Through this partnership, Northwestern is one of 15 Illinois public and private universities that will "provide scholarships to students who graduate from Chicago Public Schools, get their associate degree from one of the city's community colleges, and then get admitted to a bachelor's degree program." The partnership was influenced by Mayor Rahm Emanuel, who encouraged local universities to increase opportunities for students in the public school district. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_Illinois_University" title="Northeastern Illinois University">Northeastern Illinois University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/School_of_the_Art_Institute_of_Chicago" title="School of the Art Institute of Chicago">School of the Art Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/DePaul_University" title="DePaul University">DePaul University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Loyola_University_Chicago" title="Loyola University Chicago">Loyola University</a> are also part of the Star Scholars partnership.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries_and_museums">Libraries and museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Libraries and museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg/220px-University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg/330px-University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg/440px-University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>University Library (1970), in <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">Brutalist</a> style</div></div></div>
<p>The Northwestern library system consists of four libraries on the Evanston campus including the present main library, <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Library" title="Northwestern University Library">University Library</a> and the original library building, <a href="/wiki/Deering_Library" title="Deering Library">Deering Library</a>; three libraries on the Chicago campus; and the library affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Garrett-Evangelical_Theological_Seminary" class="mw-redirect" title="Garrett-Evangelical Theological Seminary">Garrett-Evangelical Theological Seminary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Library_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The University Library contains over 4.9 million volumes, 4.6 million <a href="/wiki/Microform" title="Microform">microforms</a>, and almost 99,000 <a href="/wiki/Periodical" class="mw-redirect" title="Periodical">periodicals</a> making it (by volume) the 30th-largest university library in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> and the 10th-largest library among private universities.<sup id="cite_ref-Library_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Library_Stats_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library_Stats-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Notable collections in the library system include the <a href="/wiki/Melville_J._Herskovits" title="Melville J. Herskovits">Melville J. Herskovits</a> Library of African Studies, the largest <a href="/wiki/Africana_studies" title="Africana studies">Africana</a> collection in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> an extensive collection of early edition printed music and <a href="/wiki/Manuscript" title="Manuscript">manuscripts</a> as well as late-modern works, and an art collection noted for its 19th and 20th-century <a href="/wiki/Western_art_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Western art history">Western art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Architecture_criticism" title="Architecture criticism">architecture periodicals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LibraryPR_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LibraryPR-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The library system participates with 15 other universities in digitizing its collections as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Google_Book_Search" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Book Search">Google Book Search</a> project.<sup id="cite_ref-LibraryPR_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LibraryPR-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mary_and_Leigh_Block_Museum_of_Art" title="Mary and Leigh Block Museum of Art">Mary and Leigh Block Museum of Art</a> is a major <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_and_cultural_institutions_in_Chicago#Art" title="List of museums and cultural institutions in Chicago">art museum in Chicago</a>, containing more than 4,000 works in its permanent collection as well as dedicating a third of its space to temporary and traveling exhibitions.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_Educational_Foundation" title="Holocaust Educational Foundation">Holocaust Educational Foundation</a>, which had previously endowed the Theodore Zev Weiss – Holocaust Educational Foundation Professorship in <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_Studies" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust Studies">Holocaust Studies</a>, became part of Northwestern.<sup id="cite_ref-NWHF_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NWHF-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HF_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HF-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg/220px-Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg/330px-Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg/440px-Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ford Motor Company Engineering Design Center (2005)</div></div></div>
<p>Northwestern was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> in 1917 and remains a research university with "very high" research activity.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_94-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AAU_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AAU-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern's schools of management, engineering, and communication are among the most academically productive in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-FSPI_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FSPI-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern received $649.7 million in research funding in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern supports nearly 1,500 research laboratories across two campuses, predominately in the medical and biological sciences. Through the Innovation and New Ventures Office (INVO),<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern researchers disclosed 247 inventions, filed 270 patent applications, received 81 foreign and US patents, started 12 companies, and generated $79.8 million in licensing revenue in 2013. The bulk of the revenue has come from a patent on pregabalin, a synthesized organic molecule discovered by chemistry professor <a href="/wiki/Richard_Bruce_Silverman" title="Richard Bruce Silverman">Richard Silverman</a>, which ultimately was marketed as <a href="/wiki/Lyrica" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyrica">Lyrica</a>, a drug sold by <a href="/wiki/Pfizer" title="Pfizer">Pfizer</a>, to combat epilepsy, neuropathic pain, and fibromyalgia. INVO has been involved in creating a number of centers, including the Center for Developmental Therapeutics (CDT)<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> and the Center for Device Development (CD2).<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> It has also helped form over 50 startup companies based on Northwestern technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Northwestern is home to the Center for Interdisciplinary Exploration and Research in Astrophysics, Northwestern Institute for Complex Systems, Nanoscale Science and Engineering Center, Materials Research Center, Center for Quantum Devices, Institute for Policy Research, International Institute for Nanotechnology, Center for Catalysis and Surface Science, Buffet Center for International and Comparative Studies, the Initiative for Sustainability and Energy at Northwestern<sup id="cite_ref-ISEN_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISEN-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Argonne/Northwestern_Solar_Energy_Research_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Argonne/Northwestern Solar Energy Research Center">Argonne/Northwestern Solar Energy Research Center</a> and other centers for interdisciplinary research.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_life">Campus life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Campus life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg/220px-Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg/330px-Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg/440px-Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2463" data-file-height="1821" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Rock in front of University Hall</div></div></div>
<p>The undergraduates have a number of traditions: Painting <a href="/wiki/The_Rock_(Northwestern_University)" title="The Rock (Northwestern University)">The Rock</a> (originally a fountain donated by the Class of 1902) is a way to advertise, for example, campus organizations, events in Greek life, student groups, and university-wide events.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Dance_Marathon" title="Northwestern University Dance Marathon">Dance Marathon</a>, a 30-hour philanthropic event, has raised more than 13 million dollars in its history for various children's charities.<sup id="cite_ref-NUDM_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NUDM-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> <i>Primal Scream</i> is held at 9 p.m. on the Sunday before finals week every quarter; students lean out of windows or gather in courtyards and scream.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Armadillo Day, or, more popularly, <a href="/wiki/Dillo_Day" title="Dillo Day">Dillo Day</a>, a day of music and food, is held on Northwestern's <a href="/wiki/Lakefill" class="mw-redirect" title="Lakefill">Lakefill</a> every Spring on the weekend after <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Day" title="Memorial Day">Memorial Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>  And in one of the university's newer traditions, every year during freshman orientation, known as Wildcat Welcome, freshmen and transfer students pass through Weber Arch to the loud huzzahs of upperclassmen and the music of the University Marching Band, known as March through the Arch.
</p><p>There are traditions long associated with <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_football" title="Northwestern Wildcats football">football</a> games. Students growl like wildcats when the opposing team controls the ball, while simulating a paw with their hands. They will also jingle keys at the beginning of each kickoff. In the past, before the tradition was discontinued, students would throw marshmallows during games.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The Clock Tower at the Rebecca Crown Center glows purple, instead of its usual white, after a winning game, thereby proclaiming the happy news. The Clock Tower remains purple until a loss or until the end of the sports season. Whereas formerly the Clock Tower was lighted only for football victories, wins for <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball" title="Northwestern Wildcats men&#39;s basketball">men's basketball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_women%27s_lacrosse" title="Northwestern Wildcats women&#39;s lacrosse">women's lacrosse</a> now merit commemoration as well; important victories in other sports may also prompt an empurpling.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Performing arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Two annual productions are especially notable: <a href="/wiki/The_Waa-Mu_Show" title="The Waa-Mu Show">The Waa-Mu Show</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Dolphin_show" class="mw-redirect" title="Dolphin show">Dolphin show</a>. Waa-Mu is an original musical, written and produced almost entirely by students.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Children's theater is represented on campus by Griffin's Tale and Purple Crayon Players.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Its umbrella organization — the Student Theatre Coalition, or StuCo — organizes nine student theater companies, multiple performance groups and more than sixty independent productions each year.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Many Northwestern alumni have used these productions as stepping stones to successful television and film careers. Chicago's <a href="/wiki/Lookingglass_Theatre_Company" title="Lookingglass Theatre Company">Lookingglass Theatre Company</a>, for example, which began life in the Great Room in <a href="/wiki/Jones_Residential_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Jones Residential College">Jones Residential College</a>, was founded in 1988 by several alumni, including <a href="/wiki/David_Schwimmer" title="David Schwimmer">David Schwimmer</a>; in 2011, it won the Regional Tony Award.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Northwestern also has a variety of improvisational groups. The improv and <a href="/wiki/Sketch_comedy" title="Sketch comedy">sketch comedy</a> group Mee-Ow created by Paul Warshauer and Josh Lazar in 1974 lists <a href="/wiki/Julia_Louis-Dreyfus" title="Julia Louis-Dreyfus">Julia Louis-Dreyfus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ana_Gasteyer" title="Ana Gasteyer">Ana Gasteyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dermot_Mulroney" title="Dermot Mulroney">Dermot Mulroney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seth_Meyers" title="Seth Meyers">Seth Meyers</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Cameron_Mitchell" title="John Cameron Mitchell">John Cameron Mitchell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kristen_Schaal" title="Kristen Schaal">Kristen Schaal</a> among its alumni.
</p><p>The undergraduate students maintain twelve <a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a> groups, including THUNK a cappella, the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Undertones" title="Northwestern Undertones">Northwestern Undertones</a>, ShireiNU A Cappella, and Purple Haze.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Northwestern's <a href="/wiki/Mock_Trial" class="mw-redirect" title="Mock Trial">Mock Trial</a> team had two teams qualify for the 2018 National Championship Tournament hosted by the American Mock Trial Association, making Northwestern one of seven schools in the nation to be represented by multiple teams at this competition.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>  One of these teams finished 9th in their division and is ranked 20th in the country out of roughly 750 teams for the 2018–2019 season.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Debate_society">Debate society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Debate society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Northwestern Debate Society is a <a href="/wiki/Policy_debate" title="Policy debate">policy debate</a> team which has won fifteen <a href="/wiki/National_Debate_Tournament" title="National Debate Tournament">National Debate Tournaments</a>, the highest number of any university. Famous alumni of the society include <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Chemerinsky" title="Erwin Chemerinsky">Erwin Chemerinsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elliot_Mincberg" title="Elliot Mincberg">Elliot Mincberg</a>, the latter senior vice president, general counsel and legal director of <a href="/wiki/People_For_the_American_Way" class="mw-redirect" title="People For the American Way">People For the American Way</a>. Scott Deatherage, the head coach, was named "Coach of the Nineties".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Service">Service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many students are involved in community service in one form or another. Annual events include <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Dance_Marathon" title="Northwestern University Dance Marathon">Dance Marathon</a>, a thirty-hour event that raised more than a million dollars for charity in 2011;<sup id="cite_ref-NUDM_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NUDM-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> and Project Pumpkin, a <a href="/wiki/Halloween" title="Halloween">Halloween</a> celebration hosted by the Northwestern Community Development Corps (NCDC) to which more than 800 local children are invited for an afternoon of games and sweets. NCDC's work is to connect hundreds of student volunteers to some twenty volunteer sites in Evanston and Chicago throughout the year.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Many students have assisted with the <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a> and have taken <a href="/wiki/Alternative_break" title="Alternative break">alternative spring break</a> trips to hundreds of service sites across the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern students also participate in the Freshman Urban Program, a program for students interested in community service.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> A large and growing number of students participate in the university's Global Engagement Studies Institute (GESI), a group service-learning expedition in Asia, Africa, or Latin America, in conjunction with the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Foundation_for_Sustainable_Development&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Foundation for Sustainable Development (page does not exist)">Foundation for Sustainable Development</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Several internationally recognized <a href="/wiki/International_nongovernmental_organization" class="mw-redirect" title="International nongovernmental organization">non-profit organizations</a> have originated at Northwestern including the <a href="/wiki/WHIA" class="mw-redirect" title="WHIA">World Health Imaging, Informatics and Telemedicine Alliance</a>, a spin-off from an engineering student's <a href="/wiki/Honors_course" class="mw-redirect" title="Honors course">honors</a> <a href="/wiki/Thesis" title="Thesis">thesis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Undergraduate_housing">Undergraduate housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Undergraduate housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_residences" title="List of Northwestern University residences">List of Northwestern University residences</a></div>
<p>Northwestern has several housing options, including both traditional residence halls and residential colleges which gather together students who have a particular intellectual interest in common. Among the residential colleges are the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_residences#Residential_College_of_Cultural_and_Community_Studies_(CCS)" title="List of Northwestern University residences">Residential College of Cultural and Community Studies (CCS)</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_residences#Thomas_G._Ayers_College_of_Commerce_and_Industry" title="List of Northwestern University residences">Ayers College of Commerce and Industry</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_residences#Jones_Fine_and_Performing_Arts_Residential_College" title="List of Northwestern University residences">Jones Residential College (Arts)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_residences#Slivka_Residential_College_for_Science_and_Engineering" title="List of Northwestern University residences">Slivka Residential College (Science and Engineering)</a>. Dorms include 1835 Hinman, Bobb-McCulloch, Foster-Walker complex (commonly referred to as Plex), Elder Hall and several more.
</p><p>In the winter of 2013, 39% of undergraduates were affiliated with a <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities">fraternity</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sorority" class="mw-redirect" title="Sorority">sorority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Northwestern recognizes 21 fraternities and 18 sororities.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Print">Print</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Print">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Northwestern" title="The Daily Northwestern">The Daily Northwestern</a></i> is the main student newspaper. Established in 1881, and published on weekdays during the academic year, it is directed entirely by undergraduates. Although it serves the Northwestern community, the <i>Daily</i> has no business ties to the university, and is supported wholly by advertisers. It is owned by the Students Publishing Company.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/North_by_Northwestern" title="North by Northwestern">North by Northwestern</a></i> is an online undergraduate magazine established in September 2006 by students at the Medill School of Journalism. Published on weekdays, it consists of updates on news stories and special events inserted throughout the day and on weekends. It also publishes a quarterly print magazine.
</p><p><i>Syllabus</i> is the undergraduate yearbook. First published in 1885, the yearbook is an epitome of that year's events at Northwestern. Published by Students Publishing Company and edited by Northwestern students, it is distributed in late May.
</p><p><i>Northwestern Flipside</i> is an undergraduate satirical magazine. Founded in 2009, it publishes a weekly issue both in print and online.
</p><p><i>Helicon</i> is the university's undergraduate literary magazine. Started in 1979, it is published twice a year: a web issue in the winter, and a print issue with a web complement in the spring.
</p><p><i>The Protest</i> is Northwestern's quarterly social justice magazine.
</p><p>The Northwestern division of Student Multicultural Affairs also supports publications such as <i>NUAsian,</i> a magazine and blog about Asian and Asian-American culture and issues; <i>Ahora,</i> a magazine about Hispanic and Latino/a culture and campus life; <i>BlackBoard Magazine</i>, about African-American life; and <i>Al Bayan</i>,  published by the Northwestern Muslim-cultural Student Association.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Law_Review" title="Northwestern University Law Review">Northwestern University Law Review</a></i> is a scholarly legal publication and student organization at <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Northwestern University School of Law">Northwestern University School of Law</a>. Its primary purpose is to publish a journal of broad legal scholarship. The <i>Law Review</i> publishes six issues each year. Student editors make the editorial and organizational decisions and select articles submitted by professors, judges, and practitioners, as well as student pieces.  The <i>Law Review</i> recently extended its presence onto the web, and now publishes scholarly pieces weekly on the <i><a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Law_Review_Colloquy" title="Northwestern University Law Review Colloquy">Colloquy</a></i>.
</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Journal_of_Technology_and_Intellectual_Property" title="Northwestern Journal of Technology and Intellectual Property">Northwestern Journal of Technology and Intellectual Property</a></i> is a <a href="/wiki/Law_review" title="Law review">law review</a> published by an independent student organization at Northwestern University School of Law. The current <a href="/wiki/Editor-in-chief" title="Editor-in-chief">editor-in-chief</a> is Aisha Lavinier.
</p><p>The <i>Northwestern Interdisciplinary Law Review</i> is a scholarly legal publication published annually by an editorial board of Northwestern undergraduates. Its mission is to publish interdisciplinary legal research, drawing from fields such as history, literature, economics, philosophy, and art. Founded in 2008, the journal features articles by professors, law students, practitioners, and undergraduates. It is funded by the Buffett Center for International and Comparative Studies and the Office of the Provost.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Web-based">Web-based</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Web-based">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sherman Ave is a humor website that went online in January 2011. It often publishes content about Northwestern student life,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> and most of its staff writers are current Northwestern undergraduates writing under various pseudonyms. The website is popular among students for its interviews of prominent campus figures,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> its "Freshman Guide",<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> its live-tweeting coverage of football games,<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> and its satiric campaign in the autumn of 2012 to end the <a href="/wiki/Vanderbilt_University" title="Vanderbilt University">Vanderbilt University</a> football team's custom of clubbing baby seals.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Politics &amp; Policy is dedicated to the analysis of current events and public policy. Begun in 2010 by students in the Weinberg College of Arts and Sciences, School of Communication, and Medill School of Journalism, Politics &amp; Policy reaches students on more than 250 college campuses around the world. Run entirely by undergraduates, it is published several times a week and features material ranging from short summaries of events to extended research pieces. The publication is financed in part by the Buffett Center.
</p><p><i>Northwestern Business Review</i> is the campus source for business news. Founded in 2005, it has an online presence as well as a quarterly print schedule.
</p><p><i>TriQuarterly Online</i> (formerly <i><a href="/wiki/TriQuarterly" title="TriQuarterly">TriQuarterly</a></i>) is a literary magazine published twice a year featuring poetry, fiction, nonfiction, drama, literary essays, reviews, a blog, and graphic art.
</p><p><i>The Queer Reader</i> is Northwestern's first radical feminist and LGBTQ+ publication.
</p>
<h3><span id="Radio.2C_film.2C_and_television"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio,_film,_and_television">Radio, film, and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Radio, film, and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/WNUR" class="mw-redirect" title="WNUR">WNUR</a> (89.3 <a href="/wiki/FM_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="FM radio">FM</a>) is a 7,200-watt <a href="/wiki/Radio_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio station">radio station</a> that broadcasts to Chicago and its northern suburbs. WNUR's programming consists of music—jazz, classical, rock—varsity sports (football, men's and women's basketball, baseball, softball, and women's lacrosse),  breaking news on weekdays, politics, current events, and literature.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Studio 22 is Northwestern's student-run production company which produces roughly ten films per year. The organization, for example, financed the first film <a href="/wiki/Zach_Braff" title="Zach Braff">Zach Braff</a> directed and has produced many films in which students who would go on to successful acting careers performed, including Zach Gilford of the television show <i><a href="/wiki/Friday_Night_Lights_(TV_series)" title="Friday Night Lights (TV series)">Friday Night Lights</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-IMDB_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMDB-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Applause for a Cause</i> is currently the only student-run production company in the nation to create a feature-length film for charity. It was founded at Northwestern in 2010 and has raised over $5,000 for various local and national organizations across the United States to date.
</p><p><i>Northwestern News Network</i> is the student television news and sports network at Northwestern, serving Northwestern and <a href="/wiki/Evanston,_Illinois" title="Evanston, Illinois">Evanston</a>. Its studios and newsroom are located on the fourth floor of the McCormick Tribune Center on Northwestern's Evanston campus. NNN is funded by the Medill School of Journalism.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats" title="Northwestern Wildcats">Northwestern Wildcats</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2005_NCAA_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Championship_-_Virginia_Cavaliers_vs_Northwestern_Wildcats.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/2005_NCAA_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Championship_-_Virginia_Cavaliers_vs_Northwestern_Wildcats.jpg/170px-2005_NCAA_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Championship_-_Virginia_Cavaliers_vs_Northwestern_Wildcats.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/2005_NCAA_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Championship_-_Virginia_Cavaliers_vs_Northwestern_Wildcats.jpg/255px-2005_NCAA_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Championship_-_Virginia_Cavaliers_vs_Northwestern_Wildcats.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/2005_NCAA_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Championship_-_Virginia_Cavaliers_vs_Northwestern_Wildcats.jpg/340px-2005_NCAA_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Championship_-_Virginia_Cavaliers_vs_Northwestern_Wildcats.jpg 2x" data-file-width="611" data-file-height="700" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2005_NCAA_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Championship_-_Virginia_Cavaliers_vs_Northwestern_Wildcats.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/2005_NCAA_Division_I_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Championship" title="2005 NCAA Division I Women&#39;s Lacrosse Championship">2005 NCAA Division I Women's Lacrosse Championship</a> game between the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Cavaliers_women%27s_lacrosse" title="Virginia Cavaliers women&#39;s lacrosse">Virginia Cavaliers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_women%27s_lacrosse" title="Northwestern Wildcats women&#39;s lacrosse">Northwestern Wildcats</a></div></div></div>
<p>Northwestern is a charter member of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a>.  It is the only private institution in the conference, and has by far the smallest undergraduate enrollment (the next-smallest member, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Iowa" title="University of Iowa">Iowa</a>, is almost three times as large, with almost 22,000 undergraduates).
</p><p>Northwestern fields 19 intercollegiate athletic teams (8 men's and 11 women's) in addition to numerous club sports.<sup id="cite_ref-NU_Facts_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NU_Facts-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>  The <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_women%27s_lacrosse" title="Northwestern Wildcats women&#39;s lacrosse">women's lacrosse team</a> won five consecutive <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Championship" title="NCAA Division I Women&#39;s Lacrosse Championship">NCAA national championships</a> between 2005 and 2009, went undefeated in 2005 and 2009, added more NCAA championships in 2011 and 2012, giving them 7 NCAA championships in 8 years, and holds several scoring records.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>  The men's <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> team is recognized by the <a href="/wiki/Helms_Athletic_Foundation" title="Helms Athletic Foundation">Helms Athletic Foundation</a> as the 1931 National Champion.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> In the 2010–11 school year, the Wildcats had one national championship, 12 teams in postseason play, 20 All-Americans, two CoSIDA Academic All-American selections, 8 CoSIDA Academic All-District selections, 1 conference Coach of the Year and Player of the Year, 53 All-Conference and a record 201 Academic All-Big Ten athletes. Overall, 12 of Northwestern's 19 varsity programs had NCAA or bowl postseason appearances.
</p><p>The football team plays at <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Field_(stadium)" title="Ryan Field (stadium)">Ryan Field</a> (formerly known as Dyche Stadium); the basketball, <a href="/wiki/College_wrestling" class="mw-redirect" title="College wrestling">wrestling</a>, and volleyball teams play at <a href="/wiki/Welsh-Ryan_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh-Ryan Arena">Welsh-Ryan Arena</a>. Northwestern's athletic teams are nicknamed the Wildcats. Before 1924, they were known as "The Purple" and unofficially as "The Fighting Methodists." The name Wildcats was bestowed upon the university in 1924 by Wallace Abbey, a writer for the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Daily_Tribune" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago Daily Tribune">Chicago Daily Tribune</a> who wrote that even in a loss to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>, "Football players had not come down from Evanston; wildcats would be a name better suited to [Coach Glenn] <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Thistlethwaite" title="Glenn Thistlethwaite">Thistletwaite's</a> boys."<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The name was so popular that university board members made "wildcats" the official nickname just months later. In 1972, the student body voted to change the official nickname from "Wildcats" to "Purple Haze" but the new name never stuck.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The mascot of Northwestern Athletics is <a href="/wiki/Northwestern%27s_Willie_the_Wildcat" class="mw-redirect" title="Northwestern&#39;s Willie the Wildcat">Willie the Wildcat</a>. The first mascot, however, was a live, caged bear cub from the <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Park_Zoo" title="Lincoln Park Zoo">Lincoln Park Zoo</a> named Furpaw who was brought to the playing field on the day of a game to greet the fans. But after a losing season, the team, deciding that Furpaw was to blame for its misfortune, banished him from campus forever. Willie the Wildcat made his debut in 1933 first as a logo, and then in three dimensions in 1947, when members of the Alpha Delta fraternity dressed as wildcats during a Homecoming Parade. The <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Wildcat_Marching_Band" title="Northwestern University Wildcat Marching Band">Northwestern University Marching Band (NUMB)</a> performs at all home football games and leads cheers in the student section and performs the <a href="/wiki/Alma_Mater" class="mw-redirect" title="Alma Mater">Alma Mater</a> at the end of the game.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryan_Field.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Ryan_Field.jpg/220px-Ryan_Field.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Ryan_Field.jpg/330px-Ryan_Field.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Ryan_Field.jpg/440px-Ryan_Field.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryan_Field.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ryan_Field_(stadium)" title="Ryan Field (stadium)">Ryan Field</a>, Northwestern's 49,000 seat football stadium</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_football" title="Northwestern Wildcats football">Northwestern's football team</a> has made 73 appearances in the top 10 of the AP poll since 1936 (including 5 at #1) and has won eight Big Ten conference championships since 1903.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-National_Champs_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Champs-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> At one time, Northwestern had the longest losing streak in Division I-A, losing 34 consecutive games between 1979 and 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Streak_ends_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Streak_ends-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> They did not appear in a bowl game after 1949 until the <a href="/wiki/1996_Rose_Bowl" title="1996 Rose Bowl">1996 Rose Bowl</a>. The team did not win a bowl since the <a href="/wiki/1949_Rose_Bowl" title="1949 Rose Bowl">1949 Rose Bowl</a> until the <a href="/wiki/2013_Gator_Bowl" title="2013 Gator Bowl">2013 Gator Bowl</a>. Following the sudden death of football coach <a href="/wiki/Randy_Walker_(football_coach)" class="mw-redirect" title="Randy Walker (football coach)">Randy Walker</a> in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> 31-year-old former <a href="/wiki/All-American" class="mw-redirect" title="All-American">All-American</a> Northwestern <a href="/wiki/Linebacker" title="Linebacker">linebacker</a> <a href="/wiki/Pat_Fitzgerald" title="Pat Fitzgerald">Pat Fitzgerald</a> assumed the position, becoming the youngest <a href="/wiki/List_of_current_NCAA_Division_I_FBS_football_coaches" title="List of current NCAA Division I FBS football coaches">Division I FBS coach</a> at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1998, two former <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball" title="Northwestern Wildcats men&#39;s basketball">Northwestern basketball</a> players were charged and convicted for sports bribery as a result of being paid to <a href="/wiki/Point_shaving" title="Point shaving">shave points</a> in games against three other Big Ten schools during the 1995 season.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_football" title="Northwestern Wildcats football">football team</a> became embroiled in a different betting scandal later that year when federal prosecutors indicted four former players for perjury related to <a href="/wiki/Sports_betting" title="Sports betting">betting</a> on their own games.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> In August 2001, Rashidi Wheeler, a senior <a href="/wiki/Safety_(American_football_position)" class="mw-redirect" title="Safety (American football position)">safety</a>, collapsed and died during practice from an <a href="/wiki/Asthma_attack" class="mw-redirect" title="Asthma attack">asthma attack</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> An autopsy revealed that he had <a href="/wiki/Ephedrine" title="Ephedrine">ephedrine</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Stimulant" title="Stimulant">stimulant</a> banned by the <a href="/wiki/NCAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA">NCAA</a>, in his system, which prompted Northwestern to investigate the prevalence of stimulants and other banned substances across all of its athletic programs.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, the Northwestern women's <a href="/wiki/Soccer" class="mw-redirect" title="Soccer">soccer</a> team was suspended and coach Jenny Haigh resigned following the release of images of alleged <a href="/wiki/Hazing" title="Hazing">hazing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, the men's basketball team made earned an NCAA berth for the first time in the program's history. They won their first round matchup against Vanderbilt University, but lost to number one seed Gonzaga in the second round.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: People">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_body">Student body</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Student body">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
