<p>Northwestern enrolled 8,368 full-time undergraduate and 8,208 full-time graduate and professional students in the 2010–11 academic year, along with approximately 1,100 part-time students.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS-B_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-B-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> The undergraduate population is drawn from all 50 states and over 100 foreign countries.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS-B_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-B-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Eighty-six percent of students were graduated after four years, 92 percent after five years, the university having several five-year programs.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS-B_189-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-B-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty">Faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Faculty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_faculty" title="List of Northwestern University faculty">List of Northwestern University faculty</a>.</div>
<p>The university employs 3,401 full-time faculty members across its eleven schools,<sup id="cite_ref-Northwestern_Data_Book_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Northwestern_Data_Book-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> including 18 members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="United States National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> 65 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-acad_directory_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acad_directory-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> 19 members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> and 6 members of the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute of Medicine">Institute of Medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Notable faculty include 2010 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a>–winning economist <a href="/wiki/Dale_T._Mortensen" title="Dale T. Mortensen">Dale T. Mortensen</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> nano-scientists <a href="/wiki/Chad_Mirkin" title="Chad Mirkin">Chad Mirkin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_I._Stupp" title="Samuel I. Stupp">Samuel I. Stupp</a>; <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin_Medal_(Franklin_Institute)" class="mw-redirect" title="Benjamin Franklin Medal (Franklin Institute)">Benjamin Franklin Medal in Electrical Engineering</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Manijeh_Razeghi" title="Manijeh Razeghi">Manijeh Razeghi</a>; Tony Award-winning director <a href="/wiki/Mary_Zimmerman" title="Mary Zimmerman">Mary Zimmerman</a>; management expert <a href="/wiki/Philip_Kotler" title="Philip Kotler">Philip Kotler</a>; King Faisal International Prize in Science recipient and Nobel laureate Sir <a href="/wiki/Fraser_Stoddart" title="Fraser Stoddart">Fraser Stoddart</a>; <a href="/wiki/Steppenwolf_Theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Steppenwolf Theatre">Steppenwolf Theatre</a> director <a href="/wiki/Anna_Shapiro" class="mw-redirect" title="Anna Shapiro">Anna Shapiro</a>; sexual psychologist <a href="/wiki/J._Michael_Bailey" title="J. Michael Bailey">J. Michael Bailey</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_denier" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust denier">Holocaust denier</a> <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Butz" title="Arthur Butz">Arthur Butz</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Federalist_Society" title="Federalist Society">Federalist Society</a> co-founder <a href="/wiki/Steven_Calabresi" class="mw-redirect" title="Steven Calabresi">Steven Calabresi</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> former <a href="/wiki/Weatherman_(organization)" class="mw-redirect" title="Weatherman (organization)">Weatherman</a> <a href="/wiki/Bernardine_Rae_Dohrn" class="mw-redirect" title="Bernardine Rae Dohrn">Bernardine Rae Dohrn</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ethnographer" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnographer">ethnographer</a> <a href="/wiki/Gary_Alan_Fine" title="Gary Alan Fine">Gary Alan Fine</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>–winning historian <a href="/wiki/Garry_Wills" title="Garry Wills">Garry Wills</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a> fellow <a href="/wiki/Monica_Olvera_de_la_Cruz" title="Monica Olvera de la Cruz">Monica Olvera de la Cruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellowship" class="mw-redirect" title="MacArthur Fellowship">MacArthur Fellowship</a> recipients <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Dybek" title="Stuart Dybek">Stuart Dybek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Richeson" title="Jennifer Richeson">Jennifer Richeson</a>, Amy Rosenzweig, <a href="/wiki/John_A._Rogers" title="John A. Rogers">John A. Rogers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hersam" title="Mark Hersam">Mark Hersam</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Dichtel" title="William Dichtel">William Dichtel</a>, and Dylan Penningroth. The faculty also includes <a href="/wiki/Richard_Bruce_Silverman" title="Richard Bruce Silverman">Richard Bruce Silverman</a>, inventor of Lyrica (<a href="/wiki/Pregabalin" title="Pregabalin">Pregabalin</a>). Notable former faculty include political advisor <a href="/wiki/David_Axelrod_(political_consultant)" title="David Axelrod (political consultant)">David Axelrod</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> artists <a href="/wiki/William_Conger" title="William Conger">William Conger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judy_Ledgerwood" title="Judy Ledgerwood">Judy Ledgerwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Paschke" title="Ed Paschke">Ed Paschke</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/James_Valerio" title="James Valerio">James Valerio</a>, writer <a href="/wiki/Charles_Newman_(author)" title="Charles Newman (author)">Charles Newman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a>–winning chemist <a href="/wiki/John_Pople" title="John Pople">John Pople</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> and military sociologist and "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_ask,_don%27t_tell" title="Don&#39;t ask, don&#39;t tell">don't ask, don't tell</a>" author <a href="/wiki/Charles_Moskos" title="Charles Moskos">Charles Moskos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_alumni" title="List of Northwestern University alumni">List of Northwestern University alumni</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg/170px-CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg/255px-CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg/340px-CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2308" data-file-height="2938" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Charlton_Heston" title="Charlton Heston">Charlton Heston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>-winning actor, <a href="/wiki/National_Rifle_Association" title="National Rifle Association">National Rifle Association</a> President, B.S. '45</div></div></div>
<p>Northwestern has 225,000 alumni worldwide.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> There are notable alumni in many fields including business, government, law, science, education, medicine, media, and the performing arts. Among Northwestern's more notable alumni are U.S. Senator and presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/George_McGovern" title="George McGovern">George McGovern</a>, Nobel Prize–winning economist <a href="/wiki/George_J._Stigler" class="mw-redirect" title="George J. Stigler">George J. Stigler</a>, Nobel Prize–winning novelist <a href="/wiki/Saul_Bellow" title="Saul Bellow">Saul Bellow</a>, Pulitzer Prize–winning composer and diarist <a href="/wiki/Ned_Rorem" title="Ned Rorem">Ned Rorem</a>, much-decorated composer <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hanson" title="Howard Hanson">Howard Hanson</a>, Deputy Prime Minister of <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> <a href="/wiki/Ali_Babacan" title="Ali Babacan">Ali Babacan</a>, historian and novelist <a href="/wiki/Wilma_Dykeman" title="Wilma Dykeman">Wilma Dykeman</a>, sociologist and adviser of <a href="/wiki/CEPAL" class="mw-redirect" title="CEPAL">CEPAL</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fernando_Filgueira&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fernando Filgueira (page does not exist)">Fernando Filgueira</a>, and the founder of the presidential prayer breakfast <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Vereide" title="Abraham Vereide">Abraham Vereide</a>. U.S. Supreme Court Associate Justice <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Stevens" title="John Paul Stevens">John Paul Stevens</a>, Supreme Court Justice and Ambassador to the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Joseph_Goldberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthur Joseph Goldberg">Arthur Joseph Goldberg</a>, Chicago Mayor <a href="/wiki/Harold_L._Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="Harold L. Washington">Harold L. Washington</a> and Governor of Illinois and Democratic presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Adlai_Stevenson_II" title="Adlai Stevenson II">Adlai Stevenson</a> are among the graduates of the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Northwestern University School of Law">Northwestern School of Law</a>. Many Northwestern alumni play or have played important roles in <a href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago, Illinois">Chicago</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, such as former Illinois governor and convicted felon <a href="/wiki/Rod_Blagojevich" title="Rod Blagojevich">Rod Blagojevich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bulls" title="Chicago Bulls">Chicago Bulls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> owner <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Reinsdorf" title="Jerry Reinsdorf">Jerry Reinsdorf</a>, and theater director <a href="/wiki/Mary_Zimmerman" title="Mary Zimmerman">Mary Zimmerman</a>. Northwestern alumnus <a href="/wiki/David_J._Skorton" title="David J. Skorton">David J. Skorton</a> serves as head of <a href="/wiki/The_Smithsonian" class="mw-redirect" title="The Smithsonian">The Smithsonian</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rahm_Emanuel" title="Rahm Emanuel">Rahm Emanuel</a>, mayor of Chicago and former <a href="/wiki/White_House_Chief_of_Staff" title="White House Chief of Staff">White House Chief of Staff</a>, earned a Masters in Speech and Communication in 1985. Former lawyer, Cincinnati mayor/councilman, Ohio gubernatorial candidate, news anchor/commentator and current tabloid talk host <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Springer" title="Jerry Springer">Jerry Springer</a> is a graduate of the Northwestern School of Law. Among U.S. universities, Northwestern ranks eighth in the number of billionaires produced.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Paul_Stevens,_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/John_Paul_Stevens%2C_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg/170px-John_Paul_Stevens%2C_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/John_Paul_Stevens%2C_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg/255px-John_Paul_Stevens%2C_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/John_Paul_Stevens%2C_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg/340px-John_Paul_Stevens%2C_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2392" data-file-height="2377" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Paul_Stevens,_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Stevens" title="John Paul Stevens">John Paul Stevens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Associate_Justice_of_the_United_States_Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Associate Justice of the United States Supreme Court">Associate Justice of the United States Supreme Court</a>, J.D. '47</div></div></div>
<p>Northwestern's School of Communication has been especially fruitful in the number of actors, actresses, playwrights, and film and television writers and directors it has produced. Alumni who have made their mark on film and television include <a href="/wiki/Ann-Margret" title="Ann-Margret">Ann-Margret</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warren_Beatty" title="Warren Beatty">Warren Beatty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jodie_Markell" title="Jodie Markell">Jodie Markell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Lynde" title="Paul Lynde">Paul Lynde</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Schwimmer" title="David Schwimmer">David Schwimmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anne_Dudek" title="Anne Dudek">Anne Dudek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zach_Braff" title="Zach Braff">Zach Braff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zooey_Deschanel" title="Zooey Deschanel">Zooey Deschanel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marg_Helgenberger" title="Marg Helgenberger">Marg Helgenberger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julia_Louis-Dreyfus" title="Julia Louis-Dreyfus">Julia Louis-Dreyfus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meghan_Markle" class="mw-redirect" title="Meghan Markle">Meghan Markle</a> (later known in the United Kingdom as the <a href="/wiki/Duchess_of_Sussex" class="mw-redirect" title="Duchess of Sussex">Duchess of Sussex</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Orbach" title="Jerry Orbach">Jerry Orbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Jones" title="Jennifer Jones">Jennifer Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Megan_Mullally" title="Megan Mullally">Megan Mullally</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Cameron_Mitchell" title="John Cameron Mitchell">John Cameron Mitchell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dermot_Mulroney" title="Dermot Mulroney">Dermot Mulroney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlton_Heston" title="Charlton Heston">Charlton Heston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Kind" title="Richard Kind">Richard Kind</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ana_Gasteyer" title="Ana Gasteyer">Ana Gasteyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brad_Hall" title="Brad Hall">Brad Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shelley_Long" title="Shelley Long">Shelley Long</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Daniels" title="William Daniels">William Daniels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cloris_Leachman" title="Cloris Leachman">Cloris Leachman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Bartlett" title="Bonnie Bartlett">Bonnie Bartlett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paula_Prentiss" title="Paula Prentiss">Paula Prentiss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Benjamin" title="Richard Benjamin">Richard Benjamin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laura_Innes" title="Laura Innes">Laura Innes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Busch" title="Charles Busch">Charles Busch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_March" title="Stephanie March">Stephanie March</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Roberts_(actor)" title="Tony Roberts (actor)">Tony Roberts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeri_Ryan" title="Jeri Ryan">Jeri Ryan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kimberly_Williams-Paisley" title="Kimberly Williams-Paisley">Kimberly Williams-Paisley</a>, <a href="/wiki/McLean_Stevenson" title="McLean Stevenson">McLean Stevenson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Randall" title="Tony Randall">Tony Randall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Rae" title="Charlotte Rae">Charlotte Rae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patricia_Neal" title="Patricia Neal">Patricia Neal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Virtue" title="Tom Virtue">Tom Virtue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Dussault" title="Nancy Dussault">Nancy Dussault</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Reed" title="Robert Reed">Robert Reed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mara_Brock_Akil" title="Mara Brock Akil">Mara Brock Akil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greg_Berlanti" title="Greg Berlanti">Greg Berlanti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Nuss" title="Bill Nuss">Bill Nuss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Shor" title="Dan Shor">Dan Shor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seth_Meyers" title="Seth Meyers">Seth Meyers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Spears" title="Peter Spears">Peter Spears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_DeCaro" title="Frank DeCaro">Frank DeCaro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zach_Gilford" title="Zach Gilford">Zach Gilford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Sullivan" title="Nicole Sullivan">Nicole Sullivan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Colbert" title="Stephen Colbert">Stephen Colbert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Eichner" title="Billy Eichner">Billy Eichner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandra_Seacat" title="Sandra Seacat">Sandra Seacat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Garry_Marshall" title="Garry Marshall">Garry Marshall</a>. Directors who were graduated from Northwestern include <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Freedman" title="Gerald Freedman">Gerald Freedman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Hagmann" title="Stuart Hagmann">Stuart Hagmann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_W._Mason" title="Marshall W. Mason">Marshall W. Mason</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allison_Burnett" title="Allison Burnett">Allison Burnett</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mary_Zimmerman" title="Mary Zimmerman">Mary Zimmerman</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lee_Phillip_Bell" title="Lee Phillip Bell">Lee Phillip Bell</a> hosted a talk show in Chicago from 1952 to 1986 and co-created the <a href="/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Award" title="Daytime Emmy Award">Daytime Emmy Award</a>-winning soap operas <i><a href="/wiki/The_Young_and_the_Restless" title="The Young and the Restless">The Young and the Restless</a></i> in 1973 and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bold_and_the_Beautiful" title="The Bold and the Beautiful">The Bold and the Beautiful</a></i> in 1987. Alumni such as <a href="/wiki/Sheldon_Harnick" title="Sheldon Harnick">Sheldon Harnick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_D%27Abruzzo" title="Stephanie D&#39;Abruzzo">Stephanie D'Abruzzo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heather_Headley" title="Heather Headley">Heather Headley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kristen_Schaal" title="Kristen Schaal">Kristen Schaal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lily_Rabe" title="Lily Rabe">Lily Rabe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Walter_Kerr" title="Walter Kerr">Walter Kerr</a> have distinguished themselves on <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theater" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadway theater">Broadway</a>, as has designer <a href="/wiki/Bob_Mackie" title="Bob Mackie">Bob Mackie</a>. Amsterdam-based comedy theater <a href="/wiki/Boom_Chicago" title="Boom Chicago">Boom Chicago</a> was founded by Northwestern alumni, and the school has become a training ground for future <a href="/wiki/The_Second_City" title="The Second City">The Second City</a>, <a href="/wiki/IO_Theater" title="IO Theater">I.O.</a>, <a href="/wiki/ComedySportz" title="ComedySportz">ComedySportz</a>, <a href="/wiki/MADtv" class="mw-redirect" title="MADtv">Mad TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a> talent.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tam_Spiva" title="Tam Spiva">Tam Spiva</a> wrote scripts for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Brady_Bunch" title="The Brady Bunch">The Brady Bunch</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Gentle_Ben" title="Gentle Ben">Gentle Ben</a></i>. In New York, Los Angeles, and Chicago, the number of Northwestern alumni involved in theater, film, and television is so large that a perception has formed that there's such a thing as a "Northwestern mafia."<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Medill_School_of_Journalism" title="Medill School of Journalism">Medill School of Journalism</a> has produced notable journalists and political activists including 38 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> laureates. National correspondents, reporters and columnists such as <i>The New York Times</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span> <a href="/wiki/Elisabeth_Bumiller" title="Elisabeth Bumiller">Elisabeth Bumiller</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Barstow" title="David Barstow">David Barstow</a>, Dean Murphy, and <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Laforet" title="Vincent Laforet">Vincent Laforet</a>, <a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a>'s Gary Levin, <a href="/wiki/Susan_Page" title="Susan Page">Susan Page</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christine_Brennan" title="Christine Brennan">Christine Brennan</a>, <a href="/wiki/NBC_News" title="NBC News">NBC</a> correspondent <a href="/wiki/Kelly_O%27Donnell" title="Kelly O&#39;Donnell">Kelly O'Donnell</a>, <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS</a> correspondent <a href="/wiki/Richard_Threlkeld" title="Richard Threlkeld">Richard Threlkeld</a>, <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> correspondent <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Lapin" title="Nicole Lapin">Nicole Lapin</a>, former CNN and current <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_America" title="Al Jazeera America">Al Jazeera America</a> anchor <a href="/wiki/Joie_Chen" title="Joie Chen">Joie Chen</a>, sports broadcasting legend <a href="/wiki/Brent_Musburger" title="Brent Musburger">Brent Musburger</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> personalities <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Nichols_(reporter)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rachel Nichols (reporter)">Rachel Nichols</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Wilbon" title="Michael Wilbon">Michael Wilbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Greenberg" title="Mike Greenberg">Mike Greenberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Weissman" title="Steve Weissman">Steve Weissman</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._A._Adande" title="J. A. Adande">J. A. Adande</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Blackistone" title="Kevin Blackistone">Kevin Blackistone</a>. The bestselling author of the <a href="/wiki/A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire" title="A Song of Ice and Fire">A Song of Ice and Fire</a> series, <a href="/wiki/George_R._R._Martin" title="George R. R. Martin">George R. R. Martin</a>, earned a B.S. and M.S. from Medill.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Northwestern_Magazine_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Northwestern_Magazine-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Elisabeth_Leamy" title="Elisabeth Leamy">Elisabeth Leamy</a> is the recipient of 13 <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy awards</a> 
<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Elisabeth_Leamy_Bio_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elisabeth_Leamy_Bio-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> 
and four <a href="/wiki/Edward_R._Murrow_Award_(Radio_Television_Digital_News_Association)" title="Edward R. Murrow Award (Radio Television Digital News Association)">Edward R. Murrow Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Elisabeth_Leamy_Bio_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elisabeth_Leamy_Bio-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Feinberg_School_of_Medicine" title="Feinberg School of Medicine">Feinberg School of Medicine</a> (previously the Northwestern University Medical School) has produced a number of notable graduates, including <a href="/wiki/Mary_Harris_Thompson" title="Mary Harris Thompson">Mary Harris Thompson</a>, Class of 1870, <a href="/wiki/Ad_eundem" class="mw-redirect" title="Ad eundem">ad eundem</a>, first female surgeon in Chicago, first female surgeon at <a href="/wiki/John_H._Stroger,_Jr._Hospital_of_Cook_County" class="mw-redirect" title="John H. Stroger, Jr. Hospital of Cook County">Cook County Hospital</a>, and founder of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Hospital_for_Women_and_Children" title="Chicago Hospital for Women and Children">Mary Thomson Hospital</a>; <a href="/wiki/Roswell_Park_(surgeon)" title="Roswell Park (surgeon)">Roswell Park</a>, Class of 1876, prominent surgeon for whom the <a href="/wiki/Roswell_Park_Cancer_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Roswell Park Cancer Institute">Roswell Park Cancer Institute</a> in <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo, New York</a>, is named; <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Hale_Williams" title="Daniel Hale Williams">Daniel Hale Williams</a>, Class of 1883, performed the first successful American <a href="/wiki/Open_heart_surgery" class="mw-redirect" title="Open heart surgery">open heart surgery</a>; only black charter member of the <a href="/wiki/American_College_of_Surgeons" title="American College of Surgeons">American College of Surgeons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Horace_Mayo" title="Charles Horace Mayo">Charles Horace Mayo</a>, Class of 1888, co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Mayo_Clinic" title="Mayo Clinic">Mayo Clinic</a>; <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Montezuma" title="Carlos Montezuma">Carlos Montezuma</a>, Class of 1889, one of the first Native Americans to receive a <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">Doctor of Medicine</a> degree from any school, and founder of the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_American_Indians" title="Society of American Indians">Society of American Indians</a>; <a href="/wiki/Howard_T._Ricketts" class="mw-redirect" title="Howard T. Ricketts">Howard T. Ricketts</a>, Class of 1897, who discovered bacteria of the genus <a href="/wiki/Rickettsia" title="Rickettsia">Rickettsia</a>, and identified the cause and methods of transmission of <a href="/wiki/Rocky_mountain_spotted_fever" class="mw-redirect" title="Rocky mountain spotted fever">rocky mountain spotted fever</a>; <a href="/wiki/Allen_B._Kanavel" title="Allen B. Kanavel">Allen B. Kanavel</a>, Class of 1899, founder, regent, and president of the American College of Surgeons, internationally recognized as the founder of modern hand and peripheral nerve surgery; <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Furchgott" title="Robert F. Furchgott">Robert F. Furchgott</a>, Class of 1940, recipient of a <a href="/wiki/Lasker_Award" title="Lasker Award">Lasker Award</a> in 1996 and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="List of Nobel laureates in Physiology or Medicine">1998 Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine</a> for his co-discovery of <a href="/wiki/Nitric_oxide" title="Nitric oxide">nitric oxide</a>; <a href="/wiki/Thomas_E._Starzl" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas E. Starzl">Thomas E. Starzl</a>, Class of 1952, who performed the first successful liver transplant in 1967 and received the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a> in 2004 and a Lasker Award in 2012; <a href="/wiki/Joseph_P._Kerwin" title="Joseph P. Kerwin">Joseph P. Kerwin</a>, first physician in space, flew on the <a href="/wiki/Skylab_2" title="Skylab 2">Skylab 2</a> mission and later served as director of Space and Life Sciences at <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>; <a href="/wiki/Richard_Schlegel" title="Richard Schlegel">C. Richard Schlegel</a>, Class of 1972, developed the dominant patent for a <a href="/wiki/HPV_vaccine" title="HPV vaccine">vaccine</a> against <a href="/wiki/Human_papillomavirus" class="mw-redirect" title="Human papillomavirus">human papillomavirus</a> (administered as <a href="/wiki/Gardasil" title="Gardasil">Gardasil</a>) to prevent <a href="/wiki/Cervical_cancer" title="Cervical cancer">cervical cancer</a>; <a href="/wiki/David_J._Skorton" title="David J. Skorton">David J. Skorton</a>, Class of 1974, <a href="/wiki/Cardiologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardiologist">cardiologist</a> who became president of <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a> in 2006; and Andrew E. Senyei, Class of 1979, inventor, venture capitalist, and entrepreneur, founder of biotech and genetics companies, and a university trustee.
</p><p>Northwestern alumni involved in music include <a href="/wiki/Steve_Albini" title="Steve Albini">Steve Albini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Tyra" title="Thomas Tyra">Thomas Tyra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Bird" title="Andrew Bird">Andrew Bird</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Davine" title="Robert Davine">Robert Davine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Radin" title="Joshua Radin">Joshua Radin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Augusta_Read_Thomas" title="Augusta Read Thomas">Augusta Read Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Harry_Trythall" title="Gilbert Harry Trythall">Gilbert Harry Trythall</a>, members of <a href="/wiki/Arcade_Fire" title="Arcade Fire">Arcade Fire</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Lawrence_Arms" title="The Lawrence Arms">The Lawrence Arms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chavez_(band)" title="Chavez (band)">Chavez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dawen" title="Dawen">Dawen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/OK_Go" title="OK Go">OK Go</a>.
</p><p>Northwestern alumni involved in athletics include sprinter <a href="/wiki/Betty_Robinson" title="Betty Robinson">Betty Robinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Sund" title="Rick Sund">Rick Sund</a> (NBA), <a href="/wiki/Billy_McKinney_(basketball)" title="Billy McKinney (basketball)">Billy McKinney</a> (NBA), <a href="/wiki/Mark_Loretta" title="Mark Loretta">Mark Loretta</a> (MLB), <a href="/wiki/Joe_Girardi" title="Joe Girardi">Joe Girardi</a> (MLB), <a href="/wiki/Luis_Castillo_(American_football)" title="Luis Castillo (American football)">Luis Castillo</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Adams_(American_football)" title="Ernie Adams (American football)">Ernie Adams</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Paddy_Driscoll" title="Paddy Driscoll">Paddy Driscoll</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Otto_Graham" title="Otto Graham">Otto Graham</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Mike_Adamle" title="Mike Adamle">Mike Adamle</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Mike_Kafka" title="Mike Kafka">Mike Kafka</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Siemian" title="Trevor Siemian">Trevor Siemian</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Luke_Johnsos" title="Luke Johnsos">Luke Johnsos</a> (NFL), six-time Olympic medalist <a href="/wiki/Matt_Grevers" title="Matt Grevers">Matt Grevers</a>, Irv Cross (NFL) and PGA Tour star <a href="/wiki/Luke_Donald" title="Luke Donald">Luke Donald</a>.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-Charter-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Charter_22-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.library.northwestern.edu/archives/nu_charter.pdf">"The Northwestern University Charter and Amendments"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. Northwestern University<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 5,</span> 2007</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=The+Northwestern+University+Charter+and+Amendments&amp;rft.pub=Northwestern+University&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.library.northwestern.edu%2Farchives%2Fnu_charter.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANorthwestern+University" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Northwestern-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Northwestern_23-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.northwestern.edu/magazine/northwestern/summer2002/features/coverstory/index.htm">"Keeping the Faith"</a>. Northwestern<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">July 20,</span> 2007</span>. <q>Northwestern's own religious identity stretches back to its genesis. The University began with a prayer&#160;— the school's nine founders (all of them Methodists, three of them ministers) knelt in worship before launching their first organizational meeting. During that meeting, they agreed to establish a university under the patronage of the Methodist Episcopal Church. Through most of its history, Northwestern kept a strong Methodist tie. Regional church conferences chose a member of the board of trustees, and until 1890 every University president was an ordained Methodist minister.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Keeping+the+Faith&amp;rft.pub=Northwestern&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.northwestern.edu%2Fmagazine%2Fnorthwestern%2Fsummer2002%2Ffeatures%2Fcoverstory%2Findex.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANorthwestern+University" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Planning_a_university-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Planning_a_university_24-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nu150.northwestern.edu/news/stories/10_21_00_founders.html">"Planning a university to serve the Northwest Territory"</a>. Northwestern University<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 15,</span> 2013</span>. <q>Although the founders were strong Methodists — three of them were Methodist ministers and before the meeting all those in attendance joined in prayer — they also firmly believed that Northwestern should be institution that would serve all people. At that time in history, particularly in the Midwest, many religious denominations founded colleges aimed at educating only members of their religion.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Planning+a+university+to+serve+the+Northwest+Territory&amp;rft.pub=Northwestern+University&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.nu150.northwestern.edu%2Fnews%2Fstories%2F10_21_00_founders.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANorthwestern+University" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>

</li>
<li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFWilliamsonWild1976">Williamson &amp; Wild 1976</a>, pp.&#160;6</span>
